First Argument: Inconsistency in Affirming One Partner
First argument exposing inconsistency in Magian partnership claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Magians' claim of a single partner for God logically entails affirming countless partners.

Core Idea
One partner leads to infinite partners.

The Magians claim that only one partner exists alongside God in creation. Yet, by attributing any creative power to that partner, they open the door to countless partners, because any effect can be multiplied. This argument exposes the internal contradiction in their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice how it presents the Magian claim and then the refutation in one sentence.
The argument is concise but powerful.
2
Identify the Magian claim
The Magians affirm only one partner for the Maker. Understand that this is their stated position.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation states that by affirming any partner, they actually affirm countless partners. Think about why: if a partner can create some things, why not many?
The argument assumes that if one partner is allowed, there is no principle limiting the number of partners.
4
Reflect on the logical implication
Consider that the Magians' own principle (allowing a partner) leads to an absurd multiplication of partners. This is a reductio ad absurdum.
This shows the irrationality of their dualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها: أن المجوس لا تثبت للصانع إلا شريكاً واحداً، وهو أثبت ما لا يحصى من الشركاء. والثاني: أنه جوز وجود الفعل المحكم المتقن ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والمجوس أنكروا ذلك. وهو أثبت الله تعالى شركاء غير أحياء لا علماء ولا قادرين والمجوس لم يجوزوا ذلك. والثالث: أنه جعل صنع كل جماد وموات وأكثر من صنع الله تعالى، لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق إلا الأجسام ثم كل جسم خلقه يخلق إما باختياره وإما بالطبع ما لا يحصى من الأعراض، فيكون بمقابلته كل فرد من أجسام العالم الذي تولى الله تعالى تخليقه ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا يخلقه الله تعالى. والرابع: أن المجوس ما أضافوا إلى غير الصانع الحكيم إلا الشرور والقبائح تنزيها له، وهو كما أضاف الشرور والقبائح من الموت والسقم والمرض والزمانة والعمى والصم والعرج والشلل إلى غير الله تعالى أضاف أيضا المحاسن والخيرات من الفرح والسرور واللذة والحياة والصحة والبصر والسمع إلى غير الله تعالى، فضاهى المجوس في إضافة الشرور إلى غير الله تعالى، وأربى عليهم بإضافة الخيرات والمحاسن إلى غير الله.
First: The Magians affirm for the Maker only one partner, but he affirmed countless partners. Second: He allowed the existence of solid, precise action from one who has no life, no knowledge, no power. The Magians denied that. But he affirmed for Allah partners who are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not allow that. Third: He made the making of every inanimate and dead thing greater than the making of Allah, because Allah did not create except bodies, then each body He creates produces, either by choice or by nature, countless accidents. In contrast, each individual body of the world whose creation Allah undertook is faced with countless things that Allah does not create. Fourth: The Magians did not attribute to other than the Wise Maker except evils and ugly things, exalting Him. But he, just as he attributed evils and ugly things—death, sickness, disease, chronic illness, blindness, deafness, lameness, paralysis—to other than Allah, he also attributed beauties and goods—joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, hearing—to other than Allah. Thus he imitated the Magians in attributing evils to other than Allah, and surpassed them by attributing goods and beauties to other than Allah.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents four arguments refuting the Magian (dualist) view that associates partners with God in creation. The first argument points out that the Magians claim only one partner for the Maker, yet by allowing countless accidents from that partner, they actually affirm countless partners. The second argument shows that the Magians reject the possibility of precise action from a lifeless, powerless being, yet the proponent of this view (i.e., the one who attributes creation to others) affirms for God partners that are not living, knowing, or powerful—a contradiction. The third argument demonstrates that if creatures produce accidents, then the making of every inanimate and dead thing becomes greater than God's making, since God only creates bodies, and bodies generate countless accidents by nature or choice. The fourth argument notes that the Magians only attribute evils to other than God to exonerate Him, but the proponent goes further by also attributing goods and blessings to others, thus both imitating and surpassing the Magians in error.

Key Takeaway
Claiming one partner for God logically implies countless partners, exposing the Magians' inconsistency.

Second Argument: Contradiction in Denying Precise Action from Lifeless Beings
Second argument highlighting self-contradiction in affirming deficient partners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second argument shows the Magians' self-contradiction by affirming partners that lack life, knowledge, and power.

Core Idea
They deny precise action to lifeless beings yet affirm such beings as partners.

The Magians reject the possibility of well-ordered action from something without life, knowledge, or power. Yet, by attributing creation to partners other than God, they affirm such deficient beings as creators. This contradiction undermines their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text. It has two parts: first the Magian denial, then the refutation showing their inconsistency.
Notice the parallel structure.
2
Understand the Magian denial
The Magians do not allow that a being without life, knowledge, or power can produce a precise, solid action. They consider it impossible.
3
See the refutation
The refutation says that the proponent (the one who attributes creation to others) affirms partners for God that are not living, knowing, or powerful. That is exactly what the Magians deny.
The Magians themselves would reject such partners, yet their system implies them.
4
Connect the dots
The argument shows that the Magians' own criteria for a creator (life, knowledge, power) are violated by the partners they implicitly accept. They contradict themselves.
This is a powerful refutation of their dualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها: أن المجوس لا تثبت للصانع إلا شريكاً واحداً، وهو أثبت ما لا يحصى من الشركاء. والثاني: أنه جوز وجود الفعل المحكم المتقن ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والمجوس أنكروا ذلك. وهو أثبت الله تعالى شركاء غير أحياء لا علماء ولا قادرين والمجوس لم يجوزوا ذلك. والثالث: أنه جعل صنع كل جماد وموات وأكثر من صنع الله تعالى، لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق إلا الأجسام ثم كل جسم خلقه يخلق إما باختياره وإما بالطبع ما لا يحصى من الأعراض، فيكون بمقابلته كل فرد من أجسام العالم الذي تولى الله تعالى تخليقه ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا يخلقه الله تعالى. والرابع: أن المجوس ما أضافوا إلى غير الصانع الحكيم إلا الشرور والقبائح تنزيها له، وهو كما أضاف الشرور والقبائح من الموت والسقم والمرض والزمانة والعمى والصم والعرج والشلل إلى غير الله تعالى أضاف أيضا المحاسن والخيرات من الفرح والسرور واللذة والحياة والصحة والبصر والسمع إلى غير الله تعالى، فضاهى المجوس في إضافة الشرور إلى غير الله تعالى، وأربى عليهم بإضافة الخيرات والمحاسن إلى غير الله.
First: The Magians affirm for the Maker only one partner, but he affirmed countless partners. Second: He allowed the existence of solid, precise action from one who has no life, no knowledge, no power. The Magians denied that. But he affirmed for Allah partners who are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not allow that. Third: He made the making of every inanimate and dead thing greater than the making of Allah, because Allah did not create except bodies, then each body He creates produces, either by choice or by nature, countless accidents. In contrast, each individual body of the world whose creation Allah undertook is faced with countless things that Allah does not create. Fourth: The Magians did not attribute to other than the Wise Maker except evils and ugly things, exalting Him. But he, just as he attributed evils and ugly things—death, sickness, disease, chronic illness, blindness, deafness, lameness, paralysis—to other than Allah, he also attributed beauties and goods—joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, hearing—to other than Allah. Thus he imitated the Magians in attributing evils to other than Allah, and surpassed them by attributing goods and beauties to other than Allah.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents four arguments refuting the Magian (dualist) view that associates partners with God in creation. The first argument points out that the Magians claim only one partner for the Maker, yet by allowing countless accidents from that partner, they actually affirm countless partners. The second argument shows that the Magians reject the possibility of precise action from a lifeless, powerless being, yet the proponent of this view (i.e., the one who attributes creation to others) affirms for God partners that are not living, knowing, or powerful—a contradiction. The third argument demonstrates that if creatures produce accidents, then the making of every inanimate and dead thing becomes greater than God's making, since God only creates bodies, and bodies generate countless accidents by nature or choice. The fourth argument notes that the Magians only attribute evils to other than God to exonerate Him, but the proponent goes further by also attributing goods and blessings to others, thus both imitating and surpassing the Magians in error.

Key Terms
المجوس (Magians)
الفعل المحكم (precise action)
شريك (partner)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the Magians deny about a being without life, knowledge, or power?
A) That it can exist.
B) That it can produce precise action.
C) That it can be a partner to God.
D) That it can be evil.

Key Takeaway
The Magians contradict themselves by affirming partners that lack the very attributes they require for action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself relying on a created thing (money, status, person) as if it has independent power, while affirming with your tongue that only Allah has power? Where in your life do you see this contradiction? What will you do today to dismantle it?
?
The Magians denied that lifeless beings can produce precise action, yet they gave them a role in creation. Are there areas in your daily life where you act as if something other than Allah has control, even though you intellectually deny it? What step will you take today to realign your trust?
?
This argument exposes a logical inconsistency in dualism. But beyond logic, it calls us to purify our tawheed. Do you truly believe that Allah alone is the Creator and Sustainer in every moment, or do you give credit to secondary causes? How can you make this belief more than just a statement?

Third Argument: Creatures' Making Surpasses God's Making
Third argument demonstrating the comparative greatness of creatures' making.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how attributing creation of accidents to creatures implies that their making is greater than God's making.

Core Idea
If creatures produce accidents, they create more than God.

If we accept that creatures produce their own accidents, then the amount of creation attributed to them exceeds God's creation. God only creates bodies, but each body produces countless accidents. This argument shows the absurd consequence of attributing any creative power to creatures.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. It is a bit longer and presents a logical consequence.
The argument uses the idea of bodies producing accidents.
2
Understand God's creation
God only creates bodies, not their accidents. This is the premise.
3
Understand creatures' production
Each body, by choice or nature, produces countless accidents. So creatures produce vastly more 'things' than God.
The argument compares the number of created entities.
4
See the absurdity
If creatures produce so much, then their making is 'greater' than God's making, which is absurd and impious.
This shows the error of attributing creation to others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها: أن المجوس لا تثبت للصانع إلا شريكاً واحداً، وهو أثبت ما لا يحصى من الشركاء. والثاني: أنه جوز وجود الفعل المحكم المتقن ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والمجوس أنكروا ذلك. وهو أثبت الله تعالى شركاء غير أحياء لا علماء ولا قادرين والمجوس لم يجوزوا ذلك. والثالث: أنه جعل صنع كل جماد وموات وأكثر من صنع الله تعالى، لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق إلا الأجسام ثم كل جسم خلقه يخلق إما باختياره وإما بالطبع ما لا يحصى من الأعراض، فيكون بمقابلته كل فرد من أجسام العالم الذي تولى الله تعالى تخليقه ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا يخلقه الله تعالى. والرابع: أن المجوس ما أضافوا إلى غير الصانع الحكيم إلا الشرور والقبائح تنزيها له، وهو كما أضاف الشرور والقبائح من الموت والسقم والمرض والزمانة والعمى والصم والعرج والشلل إلى غير الله تعالى أضاف أيضا المحاسن والخيرات من الفرح والسرور واللذة والحياة والصحة والبصر والسمع إلى غير الله تعالى، فضاهى المجوس في إضافة الشرور إلى غير الله تعالى، وأربى عليهم بإضافة الخيرات والمحاسن إلى غير الله.
First: The Magians affirm for the Maker only one partner, but he affirmed countless partners. Second: He allowed the existence of solid, precise action from one who has no life, no knowledge, no power. The Magians denied that. But he affirmed for Allah partners who are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not allow that. Third: He made the making of every inanimate and dead thing greater than the making of Allah, because Allah did not create except bodies, then each body He creates produces, either by choice or by nature, countless accidents. In contrast, each individual body of the world whose creation Allah undertook is faced with countless things that Allah does not create. Fourth: The Magians did not attribute to other than the Wise Maker except evils and ugly things, exalting Him. But he, just as he attributed evils and ugly things—death, sickness, disease, chronic illness, blindness, deafness, lameness, paralysis—to other than Allah, he also attributed beauties and goods—joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, hearing—to other than Allah. Thus he imitated the Magians in attributing evils to other than Allah, and surpassed them by attributing goods and beauties to other than Allah.

The second argument shows that the Magians reject the possibility of precise action from a lifeless, powerless being, yet the proponent of this view (i.e., the one who attributes creation to others) affirms for God partners that are not living, knowing, or powerful—a contradiction. صنع (making)
جماد (inanimate)
موات (dead)

Checkpoint
According to the third argument, what does God create directly?
A) Accidents
B) Bodies
C) Both bodies and accidents
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Attributing accident production to creatures leads to the absurd conclusion that creatures' making surpasses God's making.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve a good outcome, do you feel you produced it? How does this argument expose that feeling as an error, and what would change if you truly believed every accident is from Allah?
?
In moments of frustration when things don't go your way, do you blame your own actions or external causes? How does this argument challenge your tendency to attribute outcomes to creatures rather than the Creator?
?
If you were to live today with the conviction that every event—every accident—is from Allah alone, what would you do differently in your prayer, your work, and your relationships?

Fourth Argument: Attributing Both Evils and Goods to Others Exceeds Magian Error
Fourth argument showing that attributing goods to others is worse than Magian error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how attributing both goods and evils to others is worse than the Magians' error of attributing only evils to others.

Core Idea
Attributing goods to others is worse than attributing only evils.

The Magians attribute only evils and ugly things to other than God to exalt Him. But the proponent of partnership goes further by also attributing goods and blessings to others. This surpasses the Magians in error, as it denies God's goodness and sovereignty over all that is good.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text. It lists both the Magian practice and the worse practice of the proponent.
Note the list of evils and goods.
2
Understand the Magian position
The Magians attribute only evils to other than God to keep God pure from evil. They do not attribute goods to others.
3
Understand the proponent's position
The proponent attributes both evils and goods to others, thus imitating and surpassing the Magians.
The argument highlights the inconsistency: if you want to exalt God, why attribute goods to others?
4
See the superiority of the error
Attributing goods to others is worse because it denies God's exclusive right to goodness and blessings.
This argument refutes any form of dualism by showing it leads to greater blasphemy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

First: The Magians affirm for the Maker only one partner, but he affirmed countless partners. Second: He allowed the existence of solid, precise action from one who has no life, no knowledge, no power. The Magians denied that. But he affirmed for Allah partners who are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not allow that. Third: He made the making of every inanimate and dead thing greater than the making of Allah, because Allah did not create except bodies, then each body He creates produces, either by choice or by nature, countless accidents. In contrast, each individual body of the world whose creation Allah undertook is faced with countless things that Allah does not create. Fourth: The Magians did not attribute to other than the Wise Maker except evils and ugly things, exalting Him. But he, just as he attributed evils and ugly things—death, sickness, disease, chronic illness, blindness, deafness, lameness, paralysis—to other than Allah, he also attributed beauties and goods—joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, hearing—to other than Allah. Thus he imitated the Magians in attributing evils to other than Allah, and surpassed them by attributing goods and beauties to other than Allah.

The first argument points out that the Magians claim only one partner for the Maker, yet by allowing countless accidents from that partner, they actually affirm countless partners. The second argument shows that the Magians reject the possibility of precise action from a lifeless, powerless being, yet the proponent of this view (i.e., the one who attributes creation to others) affirms for God partners that are not living, knowing, or powerful—a contradiction. Misconception: It is acceptable to attribute only evils to others to protect God's goodness.
Correction: This argument shows that even that is wrong because it leads to attributing goods to others as well, which is worse.

Checkpoint
How does the proponent surpass the Magians according to the fourth argument?
A) By attributing only goods to others.
B) By attributing both goods and evils to others.
C) By attributing only evils to others in a different way.

?
When you achieve something good, do you truly attribute it to Allah alone, or do you subtly credit your own effort or another person? How can you train your heart to see every blessing as directly from Him, starting today?
?
The Magians at least only attributed evils to others. Are you worse by attributing both good and bad to other than Allah? Examine your speech: when you say 'I earned this' or 'my hard work paid off', are you surpassing the Magians in error?
?
This lesson shows that attributing goods to others is even more grievous. What is one specific good thing you have recently attributed to yourself or someone else? How will you correct that in your heart and tongue right now?

Mu'tazila Attribution of Acts to Creatures is Shirk
Lists miracles and refutes Mu'tazila as shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing the creation of acts to creatures leads to shirk, as shown by the miracles and the views of Bishr and the majority of Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Making creatures creators of their own acts makes them partners with Allah.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by listing several miracles—like Moses' staff turning into a snake—and declares that all of these are accidents (a'rād) in which Allah has no creative act. Claiming otherwise is kufr. He then presents the Mu'tazila position, particularly Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir and the majority, who hold that creatures create their own acts, making them partners with Allah in creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the miracles list
Read the opening sentences listing various miracles. Notice that the author calls them 'accidents' and says Allah has no creative act in them.
The author uses these to establish a baseline: only Allah creates.
2
Examine Bishr's view
Next, consider Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir's position that humans can create colors, tastes, etc. This implies multiple creators alongside Allah.
Bishr was a Mu'tazili leader.
3
Analyze the majority view
The majority of Mu'tazila extend this to every voluntary act of living beings, making even animals partners with Allah. Compare this to the Magians.
The author says they surpass the Magians in two ways.
4
Connect to the hadith
The Prophet ﷺ said 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' Reflect on how this hadith condemns the view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يثبت في العصا من الجيئة والذهاب، وفي اليد من النور، وفي الماء من الانفلاق، وفي الميت من الحياة، وفي الأكمة والأبرص من البرء، وفي الخشب من الحنين، وفي الشاه المسمومة من الكلام كل ذلك أعراض لا صنع الله تعالى فيها، والقول به كفر. وبشر بن المعتمر أحد رؤسائهم يجوز خلق اللون والطعم والرائحة والبصر والسمع والإدراك من غير الله تعالى، فيصير خالق هؤلاء شركاء الله تعالى في تخليق العالم. وجمهور المعتزلة يجعلون كل فعل حصل من أحد المخلوقين الأحياء باختيارهم مخلوقا لهم خارجا عن مقدور الله تعالى، فيكون كل كلب وخنزير وبق وبعوض شريكًا للمتعالي في العالم بعضه له ما لا قدرة الله عليه وبعضه الله تعالى، فيذهب كل منهم بما خلق، وهؤلاء الجمهور منهم بل كلهم ضاهوا المجوس وأربوا عليهم بوجهين على ما قررنا في إبطال كلام معمر، ولهذا ورد المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم 'القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة'. وإنما قلنا: إن مذهبهم يؤدي إلى القول بكون قدرته من صفات الفعل، وذلك لأن من مذهبهم أن ما يثبت ولا ينفى فهو من صفات الذات، وما يثبت وينفى فهو من صفات الفعل، ولهذا جعلوا الكلام من صفات الفعل، وحكموا بكونه محدثًا لما أنه يثبت وينفي فيقال : إنه كلم موسى عليه السلام ولم يكلم فرعون، فكذا هاهنا يقال إنه يقدر على أفعال نفسه ولا يقدر على أفعال خلقه، فتكون القدرة على قضية قولهم من صفات الفعل فيكون حادثًا، والقول بذلك كفر.
It is affirmed in the staff (the miracle of) coming and going, and in the hand (the miracle of) light, and in the water (the miracle of) splitting, and in the dead (the miracle of) life, and in the blind and leper (the miracle of) healing, and in the wood (the miracle of) longing, and in the poisoned sheep (the miracle of) speech; all of these are accidents in which Allah Most High has no creative act, and holding that is unbelief. Bishr ibn al-Mu‘tamir, one of their leaders, permits the creation of color, taste, smell, sight, hearing, and perception from other than Allah Most High, making the creators of these partners with Allah Most High in the creation of the world. And the majority of the Mu‘tazila make every action that occurs from one of the living creatures by their choice created by them, outside the power (qudra) of Allah Most High, so that every dog, pig, louse, and mosquito becomes a partner with the Most High in the world; part of it belongs to it, which Allah has no power over, and part belongs to Allah Most High, and each goes off with what it created. These majority—nay, all of them—resemble the Magians and surpass them in two ways, as we have established in refuting the speech of Mu‘ammar. For this reason the reported saying from the Prophet ﷺ has come: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' And we say: Their doctrine leads to the statement that His power (qudra) is among the attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi‘l), because their doctrine holds that what is affirmed and not negated is an attribute of essence (ṣifa al-dhāt), and what is affirmed and negated is an attribute of action. For this reason they made speech an attribute of action, and judged it to be originated (muḥdath) because it is affirmed and negated: it is said that He spoke to Moses عليه السلام and did not speak to Pharaoh. So likewise here it is said that He has power over His own acts and does not have power over the acts of His creatures. Thus power, according to their claim, is an attribute of action, and therefore originated; and holding that is unbelief.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila position that creatures create their own acts. The author begins by listing several miracles (the staff of Moses, the hand of Moses, the parting of the sea, reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, the yearning of the wooden pole, and the speaking of the poisoned sheep) and notes that all these are accidents (a‘rāḍ) in which Allah has no direct creative act. To claim otherwise is kufr. Then the author mentions Bishr ibn al-Mu‘tamir, a Mu'tazili leader, who held that humans can create colors, tastes, etc. through generated acts (tawallud), making them partners with Allah in creation. The majority of Mu'tazila go further, saying every voluntary act of a living being is created by that being, outside Allah's power, thus every animal becomes a partner with Allah. The author compares them to the Magians and says they surpass them in two ways, referring to an earlier refutation of Mu‘ammar. Then the author cites the Prophet’s hadith that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this community. Finally, the author argues that this doctrine leads to saying Allah's power (qudra) is an attribute of action (ṣifa al-fi‘l), because for the Mu'tazila, what can be affirmed and negated is an attribute of action. Since Allah is said to have power over His own acts but not over the acts of His creatures, power becomes an attribute of action, hence originated (ḥādith). Holding that Allah's power is originated is kufr.

Key Terms
أعراض
مخلوق
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the miracles are examples of prophets creating, but the author uses them to show these are acts of Allah alone.
Correction: The miracles are accidents that occur by Allah's will, but they are not created by Allah in the sense of being directly produced; rather, they are manifestations of His power. The point is that no creature can create such things.

Checkpoint
Why does the author mention that each miracle is an 'accident' (arad) in which Allah has no creative act?
A) To show that Allah is not involved in miracles.
B) To argue that miracles are not created by the prophet or anyone else.
C) To prove that Allah is not omnipotent.
D) To deny the occurrence of miracles.

Key Takeaway
Attributing the creation of any act to a creature makes that creature a partner with Allah, which is shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mentally credited yourself or someone else with an achievement as if it were independent of Allah's creation? How does this passage challenge that attitude, and what step will you take today to realign your belief?
?
This passage states that every creature that acts voluntarily becomes a partner with Allah if we attribute creation of its action to it. Consider your daily interactions: do you truly believe that every movement, word, and deed of yours is only possible because Allah creates it at that moment? Or is there a residue of self-reliance? What specific thought will you use to remind yourself of this when you wake up tomorrow?
?
The hadith equates Qadariyya to Magians. If you have ever felt uneasy about divine decree or thought that your bad choices were solely your own doing, how does this categorization make you feel about the gravity of that thought? What change in your heart or speech will you commit to from now on?

intermediate
5 min
Mu'tazila Doctrine Implies Allah's Power is Created
Shows Mu'tazila view makes Allah's power an attribute of action, implying creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila view that humans create their own acts leads to the conclusion that Allah's power (qudra) is an attribute of action (sifa al-fi‘l) and therefore created, which is kufr.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila logic makes Allah's power a created attribute, which is kufr.

After establishing that the Mu'tazila view leads to shirk, Imam al-Nasafi now presents a second, more subtle argument. He shows that their own framework for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of action forces them to say that Allah's power is an attribute of action, because it is both affirmed (over His own acts) and negated (over creatures' acts). Since attributes of action are originated, this implies Allah's power is created—an outright denial of His divinity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila distinction
The Mu'tazila distinguish between attributes of essence (always affirmed) and attributes of action (affirmed in some cases, negated in others). Follow this rule.
They use this to argue that speech is an attribute of action because Allah spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh.
2
Apply to power
Now apply the same rule to power: According to Mu'tazila, Allah has power over His own acts but not over creatures' acts. Thus power is affirmed and negated, so it is an attribute of action.
This is a logical consequence of their own principles.
3
Conclude the consequence
Attributes of action are created (ḥādith). Therefore, Allah's power would be created. Holding that is kufr.
This exposes the internal contradiction in their doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يثبت في العصا من الجيئة والذهاب، وفي اليد من النور، وفي الماء من الانفلاق، وفي الميت من الحياة، وفي الأكمة والأبرص من البرء، وفي الخشب من الحنين، وفي الشاه المسمومة من الكلام كل ذلك أعراض لا صنع الله تعالى فيها، والقول به كفر. وبشر بن المعتمر أحد رؤسائهم يجوز خلق اللون والطعم والرائحة والبصر والسمع والإدراك من غير الله تعالى، فيصير خالق هؤلاء شركاء الله تعالى في تخليق العالم. وجمهور المعتزلة يجعلون كل فعل حصل من أحد المخلوقين الأحياء باختيارهم مخلوقا لهم خارجا عن مقدور الله تعالى، فيكون كل كلب وخنزير وبق وبعوض شريكًا للمتعالي في العالم بعضه له ما لا قدرة الله عليه وبعضه الله تعالى، فيذهب كل منهم بما خلق، وهؤلاء الجمهور منهم بل كلهم ضاهوا المجوس وأربوا عليهم بوجهين على ما قررنا في إبطال كلام معمر، ولهذا ورد المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم 'القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة'. وإنما قلنا: إن مذهبهم يؤدي إلى القول بكون قدرته من صفات الفعل، وذلك لأن من مذهبهم أن ما يثبت ولا ينفى فهو من صفات الذات، وما يثبت وينفى فهو من صفات الفعل، ولهذا جعلوا الكلام من صفات الفعل، وحكموا بكونه محدثًا لما أنه يثبت وينفي فيقال : إنه كلم موسى عليه السلام ولم يكلم فرعون، فكذا هاهنا يقال إنه يقدر على أفعال نفسه ولا يقدر على أفعال خلقه، فتكون القدرة على قضية قولهم من صفات الفعل فيكون حادثًا، والقول بذلك كفر.
It is affirmed in the staff (the miracle of) coming and going, and in the hand (the miracle of) light, and in the water (the miracle of) splitting, and in the dead (the miracle of) life, and in the blind and leper (the miracle of) healing, and in the wood (the miracle of) longing, and in the poisoned sheep (the miracle of) speech; all of these are accidents in which Allah Most High has no creative act, and holding that is unbelief. Bishr ibn al-Mu‘tamir, one of their leaders, permits the creation of color, taste, smell, sight, hearing, and perception from other than Allah Most High, making the creators of these partners with Allah Most High in the creation of the world. And the majority of the Mu‘tazila make every action that occurs from one of the living creatures by their choice created by them, outside the power (qudra) of Allah Most High, so that every dog, pig, louse, and mosquito becomes a partner with the Most High in the world; part of it belongs to it, which Allah has no power over, and part belongs to Allah Most High, and each goes off with what it created. These majority—nay, all of them—resemble the Magians and surpass them in two ways, as we have established in refuting the speech of Mu‘ammar. For this reason the reported saying from the Prophet ﷺ has come: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' And we say: Their doctrine leads to the statement that His power (qudra) is among the attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi‘l), because their doctrine holds that what is affirmed and not negated is an attribute of essence (ṣifa al-dhāt), and what is affirmed and negated is an attribute of action. For this reason they made speech an attribute of action, and judged it to be originated (muḥdath) because it is affirmed and negated: it is said that He spoke to Moses عليه السلام and did not speak to Pharaoh. So likewise here it is said that He has power over His own acts and does not have power over the acts of His creatures. Thus power, according to their claim, is an attribute of action, and therefore originated; and holding that is unbelief.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila position that creatures create their own acts. The author begins by listing several miracles (the staff of Moses, the hand of Moses, the parting of the sea, reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, the yearning of the wooden pole, and the speaking of the poisoned sheep) and notes that all these are accidents (a‘rāḍ) in which Allah has no direct creative act. To claim otherwise is kufr. Then the author mentions Bishr ibn al-Mu‘tamir, a Mu'tazili leader, who held that humans can create colors, tastes, etc. through generated acts (tawallud), making them partners with Allah in creation. The majority of Mu'tazila go further, saying every voluntary act of a living being is created by that being, outside Allah's power, thus every animal becomes a partner with Allah. The author compares them to the Magians and says they surpass them in two ways, referring to an earlier refutation of Mu‘ammar. Then the author cites the Prophet’s hadith that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this community. Finally, the author argues that this doctrine leads to saying Allah's power (qudra) is an attribute of action (ṣifa al-fi‘l), because for the Mu'tazila, what can be affirmed and negated is an attribute of action. Since Allah is said to have power over His own acts but not over the acts of His creatures, power becomes an attribute of action, hence originated (ḥādith). Holding that Allah's power is originated is kufr.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that attributes of action imply imperfection in Allah.
Correction: The point is that attributing createdness to any of Allah's attributes, including power, is kufr, because Allah's attributes are eternal. The Mu'tazila's own criteria force them into this false conclusion.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila criterion, what kind of attribute is power if it is affirmed in some cases and negated in others?
A) Attribute of essence
B) Attribute of action
C) Neither
D) Both

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila view that creatures create their own acts forces them to say Allah's power is created, which is kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that even a logical classification system can lead to kufr, how carefully do you examine the theological principles you hold? Are there any beliefs you accept because they 'make sense' to you, without checking if they align with revelation? What will you do to rectify that this week?
?
The Mu'tazila allowed their reasoning about speech to dictate their view of power. This shows how one mistaken analogy can corrupt multiple doctrines. Think of an area in your life where you have applied a worldly pattern to your understanding of Allah. How will you replace that with submission to what He has revealed, even if it seems less logical?
?
This passage declares that a specific view is kufr. Have you ever held a belief about Allah that, upon deeper reflection, you realize was inconsistent with His perfection? What conviction must you abandon or correct today to ensure your faith is pure?

Refuting the Mu'tazila by Applying Their Own Distinction to Divine Power
The author refutes the Mu'tazila by applying their own distinction to divine power, showing it leads to kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the Mu'tazila's own criterion for distinguishing attributes of essence and action to show that their position on divine power is either self-refuting or leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
Falsehood contradicts itself; truth coheres. Applying the Mu'tazila's own rule to power exposes their inconsistency.

The Mu'tazila claimed that some divine attributes are attributes of essence (never negated) while others are attributes of action (both affirmed and negated). They applied this to speech, arguing it is an attribute of action because God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh. But what happens when we apply the same logic to divine power? The author shows that this leads to a devastating dilemma: either power becomes an originated attribute, which is disbelief, or the Mu'tazila must abandon their own distinction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila criterion
Read the first part of the passage where the author states the Mu'tazila rule: an attribute that is affirmed and never negated is of essence; one that is both affirmed and negated is of action. Notice how they applied it to speech.
2
Apply the criterion to speech
See how the Mu'tazila concluded that speech is an attribute of action because God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh. This made them say speech is originated (hadith).
3
Apply the criterion to power
The author applies the same logic to divine power: God has power over His own acts but not over creatures' acts (according to the Mu'tazila). So power too would be an attribute of action, hence originated, which is kufr.
4
Work through the dilemma
The author presents three options for the Mu'tazila: (1) admit power is originated – contradicting their own stance; (2) say it is not originated but of essence – then they must admit power encompasses all acts, refuting their claim; (3) cling to the distinction – then they contradict themselves. Trace each option.
This shows the internal inconsistency of the Mu'tazila position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن من مذهبهم أن ما يثبت ولا ينفى فهو من صفات الذات، وما يثبت وينفى فهو من صفات الفعل، ولهذا جعلوا الكلام من صفات الفعل، وحكموا بكونه محدثًا لما أنه يثبت وينفي فيقال: إنه كلم موسى عليه السلام ولم يكلم فرعون، فكذا هاهنا يقال إنه يقدر على أفعال نفسه ولا يقدر على أفعال خلقه، فتكون القدرة على قضية قولهم من صفات الفعل فيكون حادثًا، والقول بذلك كفر. فإن زعموا أنه حادث تركوا قولهم: إنه من صفات الذات وهو قادر بنفسه، وإن زعموا أنه ليس بحادث وليس من صفات الفعل بل هو من صفات الذات وكان موصوفًا به في الأزل، فقد زعموا أن قدرته شاملة على المقدورات أجمع وقد أبطلوا قولهم: إنه لا يقدر على أفعال خلقه ورجعوا عن هذه المسألة. وإن تمسكوا بهذه المسألة وتقروا على قولهم: إن القدرة من صفات الذات، فقد أبطلوا على أنفسهم فرقهم بين صفة الذات وصفة الفعل بما ذكروا من الفرق، وإن تمسكوا بكل ذلك فقد ناقضوا أفحش مناقضة، والباطل ينقض بعضه بعضا، والحق يؤيد بعضه بعضاً، والحمد لله على العصمة من الضلالة والتمادي في الغي والجهالة.
Because it is part of their doctrine that what is affirmed and not negated is among the attributes of essence, and what is affirmed and negated is among the attributes of action. For this reason they made speech (kalam) an attribute of action, and ruled that it is originated because it is affirmed and negated: it is said that He spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, and did not speak to Pharaoh. So similarly here it is said that He has power over His own acts and does not have power over the acts of His creatures. Thus power (qudra) according to their statement becomes an attribute of action and is therefore originated, and saying that is disbelief (kufr). If they claim it is originated, they abandon their statement that it is an attribute of essence and that He is powerful by Himself. And if they claim it is not originated and not from the attributes of action but from the attributes of essence (and He was described by it in pre-eternity), then they have claimed that His power encompasses all possible things and have invalidated their statement that He does not have power over the acts of His creatures, and they have recanted from this issue. And if they adhere to this issue and affirm their statement that power is an attribute of essence, then they have nullified for themselves their distinction between the attribute of essence and the attribute of action by the distinction they mentioned. And if they adhere to all that, then they have contradicted themselves most severely. Falsehood cancels itself out, while truth supports itself. Praise be to God for protection from misguidance and persistence in error and ignorance.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila using a dilemma based on their own distinction between attributes of essence (sifat al-dhat) and attributes of action (sifat al-fi'l). The author first explains the Mu'tazila criterion: an attribute that is affirmed (yuthbat) and never negated (la yunfa) is an attribute of essence; one that is both affirmed and negated (yuthbat wa yunfa) is an attribute of action. The Mu'tazila applied this to speech (kalam), calling it an attribute of action because God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh, making it originated (hadith). The author then applies the same logic to power (qudra): God has power over His own acts but not over the acts of His creatures (according to the Mu'tazila), so power would also be an attribute of action and thus originated. But saying God's power is originated is kufr. The author then presents a dilemma: (1) If the Mu'tazila say power is originated, they abandon their claim that it is an attribute of essence and that He is powerful by Himself. (2) If they say it is not originated but an attribute of essence, they must admit that His power encompasses all acts, including those of creatures, thus refuting their own claim that He does not have power over their acts. If they cling to that claim, their distinction between essence and action attributes collapses; if they cling to both, they contradict themselves. The author concludes that falsehood is internally contradictory while truth is coherent.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Mu'tazila distinction between essence and action attributes is consistent and can be applied uniformly.
Correction: The author shows that applying it to divine power leads to either the admission that power is originated (kufr) or to an internal contradiction, exposing the distinction as self-refuting.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the consequence of applying the Mu'tazila's own criterion to divine power (qudra)?
A) Power becomes an attribute of action, and the Mu'tazila would have to say it is eternal.
B) Power becomes an attribute of action, and calling it originated amounts to disbelief (kufr).
C) Power remains an attribute of essence, and the Mu'tazila's position is strengthened.
D) The Mu'tazila distinction is shown to be irrelevant to divine power.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's own criterion, when applied to divine power, forces them into an inescapable contradiction or outright disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author thanks God for protection from misguidance. Have you ever found yourself believing something that, when you truly thought it through, contradicted a core truth of your faith? What did you do, or what should you do?
?
This lesson shows that falsehood is self-cancelling while truth is self-supporting. Where in your own understanding of God or your practice of Islam do you sense an inconsistency that you have been avoiding? Will you confront it today?
?
The Mu'tazila clung to their rational arguments even when they led to kufr. Are there any intellectual positions or habits in your life that you hold onto despite knowing they clash with the Qur'an and Sunnah? What would it cost you to let them go?

Why the Mu'tazila View Leads to Tashbih and Its Refutation
Argument that Mu'tazila view leads to tashbih and refutation of Ka'bi's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila definition of act as 'bringing from non-existence to existence' leads to problematic similarity (tashbih) between divine and human acts, and how the author refutes al-Ka'bi's objection by distinguishing essential from relative attributes.

Core Idea
Acts similar in essence cannot be differentiated by relative moral qualities.

In this passage, the author argues forcefully that the Mu'tazila definition of act as 'bringing from non-existence to existence' makes God's acts and human acts essentially identical—a form of tashbih. When al-Ka'bi objects that human acts involve submission or frivolity while God's acts are wisdom, the author counters by showing that such qualities are relational, not essential. This lesson walks through the argument and its refutation, clarifying a key Maturidi distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Absorb the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the Quranic verse quoted.
2
Identify the core claim and the objection
The author claims the Mu'tazila view necessitates similarity; al-Ka'bi objects that moral differences prevent similarity. Find these two parts.
3
Trace the refutation
Follow how the author distinguishes between the essence of an act (e.g., motion) and its relative attributes (obedience, submission). Note the examples given.
The terms 'asma' idafiyya' (relative names) are key.
4
Analyze the examples
Look at the blackness of Zayd/'Amr and the rest vs. motion examples. How do they illustrate that similarity in essence is unaffected by accidental differences?
5
Reflect on the theological outcome
Consider why this argument matters: it preserves God's transcendence while still acknowledging human acts have a real nature.
The Mu'tazila, by defining act as ikhraj, inadvertently made divine and human acts essentially the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول المعتزلة يؤدي إلى التشابه بين فعل الله وفعل العبد: وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى وقوع التشابه بين فعل القديم وفعل الحادث، فإن فعل الله تعالى لما كان إخراجًا من العدم إلى الوجود، وفعل العبد كذلك، كان كل واحد من الفعلين شبيه صاحبه خصوصا على أصلهم فإن عندهم الفعل والمفعول واحد فحركة المرتعش فعل الله ومفعوله وحركة العبد فعل العبد ومفعوله، فلا فرق بين حركة وبين حركة بمعنى من المعاني فكان فعل العبد وخلقه كخلق الله تعالى وقد قال الله تعالى: أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلَّهِ شُرَكَاءَ خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ، فَتَشَبَه الخَلْقُ عَلَيْهِمْ وهذا، والله أعلم استفهام بمعنى الإنكار والنفي، فكان الله تعالى نافيًا أن يكون من أحد خلق كخلقه. فإن قالوا: إن فعلنا وإن كان إخراجًا من العدم إلى الوجود، وفعله تعالى أيضا إخراج من العدم إلى الوجود إلا أنه لا تشابه بين فعلنا وفعله، لأن فعلنا خضوع وذلة أو عبث وفساد وفعله عز وجل حكمة وصواب وليس بخضوع ولا ذلة، والعبث لا يشبه الحكمة. هذا هو اعتراض الكعبي. يقال له: إن الحركة حركة لنفسها، وكذا السكون والسواد والبياض، وكون الفعل طاعة أو معصية أو ذلة أو خضوعاً لمعاني وراء الذات، فإن الفعل يكون طاعة لخروجه على موافقة الأمر، والمعصية تكون معصية لخروج الفعل على مخالفة الأمر وارتكاب ما نهى عنه، فكانا من الأسماء الإضافية، وكذا الحركة لا تكون ذلة لنفسها، وكذا لا تكون خضوعا لنفسها بل لقصد فاعلها، والقصد معنى في القلب والحركة تكون بالجوارح والمشتبهان لذاتيهما لا يختلفان باعتبار الأسامي الإضافية الثابتة لمعاني هي أغيار للذات. ألا ترى أن سواد زيد وسواد عمرو لا يختلفان لاختلاف المحل، وسكون زيد لا يكون مشابها لحركته وإن كان الفاعل واحدًا لاختلافهما في ذاتيهما، فإذا لم يكن لاتحاد الفاعل أثر في تشابه ما اختلفا بذاتيهما لا يكون لاختلاف الفاعل أو معنى من معانيه أو اختلاف آلة الفاعلين أثر في اختلاف شيئين اشتبها لذاتيهما، وهذا لأن
The statement of the Mu'tazila leads to similarity between the act of God and the act of the servant. And we only say that it leads to the occurrence of similarity between the act of the Eternal and the act of the originated. For the act of God, exalted, is a bringing forth from non-existence to existence, and the act of the servant is likewise. Thus each of the two acts is similar to its counterpart, especially according to their [the Mu'tazila's] principle, for according to them the act and the effect are one. So the motion of a trembling person is God's act and His effect, and the motion of a servant is the servant's act and his effect. There is no difference between one motion and another motion in any sense. So the act and creation of the servant is like the creation of God, exalted. And God, exalted, said: 'Or have they attributed to God partners who created like His creation, so that the creation became similar to them?' And this, God knows best, is an interrogative of denial and negation. So God, exalted, negated that anyone could have a creation like His creation. If they say: 'Our act, though it is a bringing forth from non-existence to existence, and His act, exalted, is also a bringing forth from non-existence to existence, yet there is no similarity between our act and His act, because our act is submission and abasement or frivolity and corruption, while His act, mighty and majestic, is wisdom and rightness, not submission or abasement. Frivolity does not resemble wisdom.' This is the objection of al-Ka'bi. It is said to him: Motion is motion in itself, and likewise rest, blackness, and whiteness. The act being obedience or disobedience, or abasement or submission, is due to meanings beyond the essence. For the act becomes obedience due to its accordance with the command, and disobedience becomes disobedience due to the act's violation of the command and commission of what was forbidden. So these are among relative names (asma' idafiyya). Similarly, motion is not abasement in itself, nor is it submission in itself, but rather due to the intention of its agent. Intention is a meaning in the heart, and motion occurs by the limbs. Two things that are similar in their essences do not differ by virtue of relative names attached to meanings that are other than the essence. Do you not see that the blackness of Zayd and the blackness of 'Amr do not differ due to difference of subject, and the rest of Zayd is not similar to his motion, even if the agent is one, due to their difference in essences? So if the unity of the agent has no effect in making similar two things that differ in their essences, then the difference of the agent or a meaning among its meanings or the difference of the instrument of the agents has no effect in differentiating two things that are similar in their essences. This is because...
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is an argument that the Mu'tazila's position leads to tashbih (anthropomorphism/similarity) between God's acts and human acts. The author begins by asserting that the Mu'tazila view necessitates similarity because both divine and human acts are defined as bringing forth from non-existence to existence. According to the Mu'tazila, act and effect are one, so the motion of a trembling person (caused by God) and the voluntary motion of a servant are identical in essence. The author cites Quran 13:16, which denies that any creature creates like God's creation, using it against the Mu'tazila. The Mu'tazila (represented by al-Ka'bi) object that acts differ in moral qualities: human acts are submission or frivolity, while God's acts are wisdom. Thus they deny similarity. The author refutes this by distinguishing between the essence of an act and its accidental attributes. An act like motion is, in itself, just motion. Qualities like obedience, disobedience, submission, or wisdom are relative (idafiyya) and depend on factors like intention and command. Since two things similar in essence do not differ due to relative attributes (e.g., two black objects remain similar in blackness regardless of the subject), the mere difference in moral quality does not negate the essential similarity of the acts as acts of bringing into existence. The author gives examples: blackness of two individuals is the same despite different subjects; rest and motion differ in essence, not by agent. Therefore, the Mu'tazila objection fails.

Key Terms
تشابه (tashabuh)
فعل (fi'l)
إخراج من العدم إلى الوجود (ikhraj min al-'adam ila al-wujud)
أسماء إضافية (asma' idafiyya)
كعبي (Ka'bi)
حركة (haraka)
ذلة (dhilla)
خضوع (khudu')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that moral differences (e.g., submission vs. wisdom) between divine and human acts prevent any similarity, so the Mu'tazila view is safe from tashbih.
Correction: The author shows that such moral qualities are relative (idafi) and do not affect the essential nature of the act. Acts similar in essence (both are 'bringing into existence') remain essentially similar regardless of these relative attributes.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute al-Ka'bi's claim that human acts (submission, frivolity) are essentially different from divine acts (wisdom)?
A) By arguing that submission and wisdom are both relative attributes that do not change the essence of the act.
B) By denying that human acts involve bringing from non-existence to existence.
C) By claiming that the Mu'tazila do not actually believe in such differences.
D) By citing a different Quranic verse that affirms the similarity.

Key Takeaway
The essential nature of an act (e.g., bringing into existence) does not change with moral qualities, which are relative and depend on intention and command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you attribute it to your own power or to God's creation? How does the Mu'tazila error of equating the essence of acts challenge your sense of humility? Will you consciously remind yourself that your ability to act is a gift from God?
?
The passage says intention (qasd) determines the moral quality of an act. Examine your own intentions: are your acts truly for God's sake, or are they tainted by seeking recognition? What concrete step can you take today to purify your intention?
?
If God's act and human act are similar in essence (both bring into existence), how does that make you view your own creative actions? Do you ever feel like you are 'creating' something independently? How can you keep alive the awareness that true creation is only from God?

The Najjariyya Principle and Essential Similarity of Temporal Things
Nasafi presents the Najjariyya principle and applies it to similarity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Najjariyya view that similarity is intrinsic, and why Nasafi affirms essential similarity among temporal things despite accidental differences.

Core Idea
Two temporal things share the same essence of origination; accidental differences do not affect their similarity.

This passage opens with a key principle of the Najjariyya school: similar things are similar by themselves, not by an added meaning. Nasafi first uses this to argue that the Creator and creatures are not similar, then shows that temporal things agree in the essence of origination. An analogy with blackness illustrates that accidental qualities do not remove essential similarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Najjariyya principle
Read the first sentence carefully. What does the Najjariyya believe about similarity?
They believe similarity is intrinsic, not by an added meaning.
2
Distinguish Creator and creatures
Notice how Nasafi applies the principle to the Creator: because the Creator is knower by Himself and creatures are not, there is no similarity.
3
Understand essential similarity among temporal things
Focus on the argument that two originated things share the same meaning of origination (ḥudūth), and differences like effort do not change that.
The blackness analogy reinforces that accidental properties do not affect essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى أصل النجارية المشتبهان مشتبهان بأنفسهما لا باشتباه هو معنى وراء المشتبهين والباري عالم بنفسه وليس المحدث عالما بنفسه، فلا يكون بينهما مشابهة على أصلهم، فأما المحدثان فلم يكونا ثم كانا فاتفقا بأنفسهما في معنى الحدوث، وقول القائل: أحدهما حدث لا بعلاج ولا تعب، والآخر حدث بعلاج وتعب، ليس بنفي الاشتباه عن المحدثين بأنفسهما إذ ليس الحدوث إلا الوجود من العدم، وهذا المعنى لا يختلف في حق حادث وحادث وإن كان أحدهما حدث بعلاج وتعب والآخر حدث لا بعلاج وتعب، إذ العلاج والتعب معنى وراء نفس الحادث ونفي معنى وراء نفس الحادث وإثبات ذلك المعنى في حق حادث لا يوجب تغيرا في ذاتيهما.
ألا ترى أن من قال: هذا سواد لزيد، وهذا سواد ليس لزيد لا الاختلاف بين السوادين ولا زوال الاشتباه، فكذا هذا.
ذلك يوجب
فإن قالوا: إن قولنا: حركة اسم عام والاشتباه يكون بالصفة الخاصة، وكونها طاعة ومعصية صفة خاصة في الحركة، لأنها تتنوع إلى الطاعة والمعصية. قلنا: قد مر إبطال هذا في مسألة التشبيه، ثم نقول: إن كون الحركة طاعة أو معصية ليس براجع إلى الذات بل ذلك اسم ثبت لورود الأمر به، فلا تغير به الصفة الراجعة إلى الذات لأن الذات لا تتغير به.
ألا ترى أن ضد الحركة وهو السكون قد يوصف بهما.
والذي يحقق هذا: اشتباه سواد زید بسواد، عمرو، ولا يقال السواد اسم عام
And according to the principle of the Najjariyya, the two similar things are similar by themselves, not by a similarity that is a meaning beyond the two similar things. And the Creator is knower by Himself, while the temporal thing is not knower by itself, so there is no similarity between them according to their principle. As for the two temporal things, they were not and then were, so they agree by themselves in the meaning of origination. And the statement of one who says: One of them came into being without treatment or effort, and the other came into being with treatment and effort, does not negate similarity between the two temporal things in themselves, because origination is only existence after non-existence, and this meaning does not differ in the case of two originated things, even if one came into being with treatment and effort and the other without, because treatment and effort are a meaning beyond the originated thing itself, and negation of a meaning beyond the originated thing and affirmation of that meaning in the case of an originated thing does not necessitate change in their essences. Do you not see that if one says: This is blackness belonging to Zaid, and this is blackness not belonging to Zaid, there is no difference between the two blacknesses nor removal of similarity. So likewise this. That necessitates. Then they said: Our saying 'movement' is a general name, and similarity is by the particular attribute, and its being obedience or disobedience is a particular attribute in the movement, because it is divided into obedience and disobedience. We said: The refutation of this has already passed in the issue of tashbih. Then we say: That movement is obedience or disobedience does not refer back to the essence, but rather that is a name established by virtue of the command regarding it, so the attribute referring to the essence does not change by it, because the essence does not change by it. Do you not see that the opposite of movement, which is rest, may be described by both? And that which confirms this: the similarity of Zaid's blackness and Amr's blackness, and it is not said that blackness is a general name.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage continues the argument by first citing the Najjariyya view that similarity is intrinsic, not by an added meaning. Nasafi uses this to distinguish between the Creator and creatures: the Creator is knower by Himself, while a temporal thing is not knower by itself, so no similarity. For two temporal things, they share the essence of origination (al-ḥudūth) – existence after non-existence. Accidental differences like treatment and effort do not affect this essential similarity; they are extra meanings that do not change the essence. An analogy: two instances of blackness remain similar in essence even if one is owned by Zaid and the other not. Then an objection: the opponent says 'movement' is a general name and similarity is by the particular attribute (being obedience or disobedience). Nasafi responds that this was already refuted in the discussion of tashbih (anthropomorphism). He reiterates that obedience/disobedience is a legal designation (due to command), not an essential attribute; the essence remains unchanged. He gives an example: rest (the opposite of movement) can be described as both obedience and disobedience, showing that the attribute is accidental. The passage ends with the same analogy of blackness to confirm the point.

Key Terms
نجارية
حدوث
ذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if two acts differ in accidental qualities like effort, they cannot be essentially similar.
Correction: Nasafi argues that essential similarity in origination is unaffected by such accidents; they are extra meanings beyond the essence.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why do two temporal things remain similar even if one comes into existence with effort and the other without?
A) Because effort is part of the essence of origination
B) Because origination (ḥudūth) is the same meaning in both
C) Because effort does not exist in temporal things
D) Because both are created by the same agent

Key Takeaway
Essential similarity in origination is not affected by accidental differences like effort.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at others who have achieved much with ease, do you secretly devalue their deeds? Can you see in them the same origin from non-being that you share, and honor that essential similarity as a gift from Allah?
?
Your own deeds—whether done with great effort or effortlessly—share the identical reality of origination. Has your pride in your hard work made you overlook that even the easiest action is a creation from nothing? Commit to seeing every deed, easy or hard, as a direct act of Allah’s bringing forth from non-existence.
?
The analogy of blackness reminds you that ownership does not change essence. You may own your actions, but their reality as temporal things is identical to the actions of others. Is there someone whose good deeds you dismiss because of their different circumstances? Will you now regard their deeds as equally originating from Allah, and remove any trace of spiritual arrogance from your heart?

Answering the Objection: Movement and Accidental Attributes
Nasafi responds to an objection about movement and accidental attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's response to the objection that 'movement' is a general name and similarity is based on particular attributes like obedience and disobedience.

Core Idea
Obedience and disobedience are legal designations, not essential attributes; they do not affect the essence of movement.

The opponent argues that 'movement' is a general term and similarity is determined by specific attributes such as obedience or disobedience. Nasafi refutes this by appealing to a previous argument, then explaining that these attributes are merely names given by command, not essential qualities. He uses the example of rest, which can be both obedience and disobedience, and the blackness analogy to show that the essence remains unchanged.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the opponent's claim: 'movement' is a general name, and similarity is by the particular attribute of being obedience or disobedience.
This sectarian objection likely comes from a group that denies essential similarity based on such attributes.
2
Understand Nasafi's response
Nasafi first says the refutation has already passed in the discussion of tashbih. Then he clarifies: obedience/disobedience do not refer back to the essence; they are names established by the command.
3
Reflect on the examples
Note the example of rest (opposite of movement) being described as both obedience and disobedience. Then the blackness analogy confirms that the general name 'blackness' does not negate similarity.

?

?

Refuting Mu'tazila: The Error of Restricting Power to Invention
Accuses Mu'tazila of ignorance for deeming possible things impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila's inability to conceive power beyond invention leads them to deem possible things impossible, and how this reflects ignorance.

Core Idea
Deeming a possible thing impossible is ignorance; deeming the necessary impossible is worse.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi directly attacks the Mu'tazila for a fundamental conceptual error. They restrict the relationship between divine power and human acts to the aspect of invention (ikhtira'), wrongly concluding that two powers cannot attach to one act. The author argues that this shows their ignorance, as they fail to consider other aspects like acquisition. By the end, we see how this mistake leads them to deny what is rationally possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's rhetorical style come through.
The passage ends mid-sentence but the key argument is complete.
2
Identify the accusation
The author begins by addressing the Mu'tazila directly. He says whoever deems a possible thing impossible is ignorant (jahil), and then strengthens: deeming the necessary impossible is even worse. Notice the escalation.
The term 'necessary' here refers to what is rationally necessary, e.g., the permissibility of two powers on one act from different aspects.
3
Pinpoint the specific error
The Mu'tazila's error is that they only conceive power's attachment to acts from the aspect of invention (ikhtira'). Their opponents agree that two powers cannot both be inventive on one act, but the real discussion is about one power being inventive and another acquisitive.
The text cuts off, but the argument is clear: the Mu'tazila conflate the aspects, leading them to deny the possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقيل لهم : لم قلتم ذلك وقد وقعت الخصومة فيه ثم ما أقمنا من الدلائل موجب ذلك ومن عد الممكن ممتنعا فهو جاهلي فكيف بمن عد الواجب ممتنعا؟ ثم هم إنما عدوا ذلك ممتنعا لأنهم لم يعقلوا تعلق القدرة بالمقدور إلا من جهة الاختراع وذلك لعمري محال وعند خصومهم قط لا يجوز تعلق قدرتين بجهة الاختراع بمقدور واحد وإنما الكلام وراء ذلك وهو أن قدرة واحدة لما تعلقت
So it was said to them: Why did you say that, while the dispute has occurred in it, and we have established proofs that necessitate it? And whoever deems the possible impossible is ignorant, so how about one who deems the necessary impossible? Then they only deemed that impossible because they did not conceive the attachment of power to the act of power except from the aspect of invention, and that, by my life, is impossible. And according to their opponents, it is absolutely not permissible for two powers to attach to one act of power from the aspect of invention; rather, the discussion is beyond that—namely, that one power when it has attached...
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a direct refutation of the Mu'tazila. The author rhetorically asks them why they hold their position despite the proofs presented. Calling someone who deems a possible thing (mumkin) impossible (mumtani') ignorant, the author intensifies the criticism: how much worse to deem a necessary thing (i.e., the permissibility of two powers on one act) impossible? The root of their error is that they only understand the relationship of power to the act of power from the aspect of invention (ikhtira'), which indeed would be impossible. But their opponents agree that two powers cannot attach from the aspect of invention. The real discussion is about one power attaching from the aspect of invention and another from acquisition. The text cuts off, but the argument is clear: the Mu'tazila have confounded the aspects.

واجب
تعلق القدرة
جهة الاختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author is saying two powers can both be creative, but he clarifies that the issue is about different aspects (creative vs. acquisitive).
Correction: The author agrees with the Mu'tazila that two powers cannot both be inventive, but argues that one can be inventive and the other acquisitive, which is possible.

Checkpoint
What is the main error the author attributes to the Mu'tazila in this passage?
A) They deny that God creates acts.
B) They only conceive power as relating to acts through invention, ignoring acquisition.
C) They reject the consensus of the scholars.
D) They claim that a single act can be created by two creators.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's error is restricting divine power to the aspect of invention, leading them to incorrectly deem impossible what is actually possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila deemed something impossible simply because they could not conceive of it. Where in your life have you rejected a possibility because it didn't fit your limited understanding of Allah's power? Will you now ask Him to expand your heart to trust in what He can do beyond your imagination?
?
The author calls those who deem the possible ignorant. Are you quick to label as 'impossible' of Allah what you have not seen or experienced? Today, identify one matter you have been despairing of—will you repent and say, 'Allah is able to do all things,' even if it requires a paradigm shift in how you think about His power?
?
This lesson reveals that the root of error is a narrow conception of divine action. What current beliefs or habits in your worship (or daily life) might be based on a restrictive view of how Allah acts? Will you study the divine names and attributes more deeply to correct this, beginning now?

Refutation of Bishr's Stone Division
Refutation of Bishr's stone division attempt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir's attempt to solve the problem of two agents moving a stone by dividing its parts is inconsistent with the assumption of equal agents.

Core Idea
Dividing the stone's parts doesn't solve the problem—it just shifts the inconsistency.

The Mu'tazilite doctrine of tawallud led to a dilemma: if two equal agents move a stone, the movement is one act attributable to both. Bishr tried to escape by dividing the stone's parts. In this passage, the author shows that Bishr's solution fails when the agents are assumed equal in all respects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how the author sets up the problem with the Ahl al-Sunna's forced argument.
2
Identify the key moves
The passage has three parts: (1) the Ahl al-Sunna's ilzām about two agents moving a stone, (2) Bishr's response dividing the stone's parts, and (3) the refutation focusing on equality of agents. Find each part.
3
Analyse Bishr's attempted solution
Bishr tries to avoid one act for two agents by splitting the stone's parts. Why does he think that helps? What does he say about even vs. odd parts?
Consider the assumption that agents are equal in all respects.
4
Understand the refutation
The author's interlocutor presses Bishr: if the agents are equal, how can one produce more movement? Bishr concedes equality is impossible. This shows the division only works if you abandon the initial assumption of equality.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
This is a classic kalam argument pattern: a forced consequence (ilzām) and an attempted escape that leads to another inconsistency. Think about why this method is effective in theological debate.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then they, with their refusal of the attachment of two powers to one thing within power from two aspects, and the consensus of all rational people on the impossibility of their attachment to it from the aspect of creation, led them their corrupt principles to permit their attachment to it from one aspect, namely creation. So the matter became grave for them, and their leaders dispersed in seeking a way out, but they could not, and they only obtained ignorance and departure from the testimonies of cognitions. And that is because the Ahl al-Sunna forced upon them, according to their statement about tawallud (generation), that if two men equal in power moved a stone and the stone moved, then what was in it of movement would be an act of both movers, a thing within power for both. So one thing would be an act of two agents, a thing within power for two powerful agents. Thus what they directed against the Ahl al-Sunna of denying a thing within power for two powerful agents, and against the theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith and al-Najjariyya of the impossibility of one thing being an act of two agents, is invalidated. Then the Mu'tazila divided in repelling this forcing (ilzām). Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir claimed that if the parts of the stone were even, half of it would move by one and the other half by the second. It was said to him: If the parts were odd, for example eleven parts? He said: Six movements from it belong to one and the five remaining to the second. It was said to him: If they were equal in build, strength, energy, and will, how can it be conceived that more is attributed to one and less to the other? He said: It is impossible that they be equal in that. So it was said to him: Why did you say that? He said: Because if they were equal in that, it would necessitate one of two things: either the existence...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazilite attempt to escape a necessary consequence of their own doctrine of tawallud (generation). The author first notes that the Mu'tazila, despite their refusal to allow two powers on one act from different aspects, were forced by their own principles to permit two powers from one aspect (creation) in the case of two agents moving a stone. This forced them into inconsistency. The Ahl al-Sunna presented a dilemma: if two equal agents move a stone, then the movement is one act attributable to both, which would mean one thing in power for two agents. This invalidates the Mu'tazila's denial of such a possibility. In response, the Mu'tazila split, and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir attempted to resolve it by dividing the stone's parts: if the number of parts is even, each moves half; if odd, one moves more than the other. The author's interlocutor then presses Bishr: if the two agents are exactly equal in all respects, it is inconceivable that one would produce more movement than the other. Bishr concedes that equality in that is impossible, but the text ends with his unfinished argument that equality would necessitate one of two things (presumably absurdities).

إلزام

زوج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That dividing the stone's parts completely resolves the problem of one act for two agents.
Correction: The division only works if agents are unequal; but the original scenario assumed equality, so the solution fails.

Checkpoint
How does Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir attempt to avoid the conclusion that one stone movement can be an act of two agents?
A) He denies that the stone moves at all.
B) He claims the stone's parts are moved by different agents.
C) He says the agents are never truly equal.
D) He invokes the concept of kasb.

Key Takeaway
Bishr's division of the stone's parts fails because it requires agents to be unequal, contradicting the initial assumption of equality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult argument that challenges your deeply held beliefs, do you find yourself making minor adjustments (like Bishr dividing the stone) to avoid the full force of the critique, rather than honestly reconsidering your entire position? Can you think of a specific instance and what it cost you intellectually or spiritually?
?
The passage reveals that even a clever escape fails if the underlying assumptions are inconsistent. Is there an area of your faith or life where you are holding onto a position that requires you to ignore or deny an obvious inconsistency? What would it cost you to admit the inconsistency and seek the truth, even if it means changing your view?
?
Bishr was forced to admit that equality of agents is impossible to avoid contradiction. Are there truths about Allah's attributes—His oneness, power, or justice—that you find uncomfortable because they seem to conflict with your human reasoning? How do you respond when your reasoning leads to a conclusion that feels difficult or mysterious?
